<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en"><span dir="auto">Kangana Ranaut</span></h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
</div>
<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="metadata topicon nopopups" id="protected-icon" style="display:none;right:55px"><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Protection_policy#semi" title="This article is semi-protected to promote compliance with the policy on biographies of living people"><img alt="Page semi-protected" data-file-height="128" data-file-width="128" height="20" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Padlock-silver.svg/20px-Padlock-silver.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Padlock-silver.svg/30px-Padlock-silver.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Padlock-silver.svg/40px-Padlock-silver.svg.png 2x" width="20"/></a></div>

<p><b>Kangana Ranaut</b> (<small>pronounced </small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Hindi_and_Urdu" title="Help:IPA for Hindi and Urdu">[kəŋɡənaː raːɳoːʈʰ]</a></span>; born 23 March 1987) is an Indian film actress. She has established a successful career in <a href="/wiki/Bollywood" title="Bollywood">Bollywood</a>, and is the recipient of a <a href="/wiki/National_Film_Awards_(India)" title="National Film Awards (India)">National Film Award</a> and <a href="/wiki/Filmfare_Awards" title="Filmfare Awards">Filmfare Awards</a> in three categories.</p>
<p>Born in Bhambla, a small town in <a href="/wiki/Himachal_Pradesh" title="Himachal Pradesh">Himachal Pradesh</a>, Ranaut initially aspired to become a doctor at the insistence of her parents. Adamant to build her own career path, she relocated to Delhi at age sixteen, where she briefly became a model. After training under the theatre director <a href="/wiki/Arvind_Gaur" title="Arvind Gaur">Arvind Gaur</a>, Ranaut made her feature film debut in the 2006 thriller <i><a href="/wiki/Gangster_(2006_film)" title="Gangster (2006 film)">Gangster</a></i>, for which she was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Filmfare_Award_for_Best_Female_Debut" title="Filmfare Award for Best Female Debut">Filmfare Award for Best Female Debut</a>. She received praise for portraying emotionally intense characters in the dramas <i><a href="/wiki/Woh_Lamhe" title="Woh Lamhe">Woh Lamhe</a></i> (2006), <i><a href="/wiki/Life_in_a..._Metro" title="Life in a... Metro">Life in a... Metro</a></i> (2007) and <i><a href="/wiki/Fashion_(film)" title="Fashion (film)">Fashion</a></i> (2008). For the last of these, she won the <a href="/wiki/National_Film_Award_for_Best_Supporting_Actress" title="National Film Award for Best Supporting Actress">National Film Award for Best Supporting Actress</a> and a Filmfare Award <a href="/wiki/Filmfare_Award_for_Best_Supporting_Actress" title="Filmfare Award for Best Supporting Actress">in the same category</a>.</p>
<p>Ranaut featured in the commercially successful films <i><a href="/wiki/Raaz:_The_Mystery_Continues" title="Raaz: The Mystery Continues">Raaz: The Mystery Continues</a></i> (2009) and <i><a href="/wiki/Once_Upon_a_Time_in_Mumbaai" title="Once Upon a Time in Mumbaai">Once Upon a Time in Mumbaai</a></i> (2010), though she was criticised for being typecast in <a href="/wiki/Neurosis" title="Neurosis">neurotic</a> roles. A comic role opposite <a href="/wiki/R._Madhavan" title="R. Madhavan">R. Madhavan</a> in the 2011 box office hit <i><a href="/wiki/Tanu_Weds_Manu" title="Tanu Weds Manu">Tanu Weds Manu</a></i> was well-received, though this was followed by a series of brief, glamorous roles in films that failed to propel her career forward. She then played a <a href="/wiki/Mutant" title="Mutant">mutant</a> opposite <a href="/wiki/Hrithik_Roshan" title="Hrithik Roshan">Hrithik Roshan</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Science_fiction_film" title="Science fiction film">science fiction film</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Krrish_3" title="Krrish 3">Krrish 3</a></i> (2013), one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_Bollywood_films" title="List of highest-grossing Bollywood films">highest-grossing Bollywood films of all time</a>, and won the <a href="/wiki/Filmfare_Award_for_Best_Actress" title="Filmfare Award for Best Actress">Filmfare Award for Best Actress</a> for playing the protagonist of the comedy-drama <i><a href="/wiki/Queen_(film)" title="Queen (film)">Queen</a></i> (2014). These accomplishments established her as a leading actress of Hindi cinema.</p>
<p>Ranaut is particularly known in the media for expressing her honest opinions in public, and is frequently credited as one of the most fashionable Indian celebrities.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life_and_background">Early life and background</span></h2>
<p>Ranaut was born on 23 March 1987 at Bhambla (now Surajpur), a small town in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mandi,_Himachal_Pradesh,_India" title="Mandi, Himachal Pradesh, India">Mandi district</a> of <a href="/wiki/Himachal_Pradesh" title="Himachal Pradesh">Himachal Pradesh</a>, into a <a href="/wiki/Rajput" title="Rajput">Rajput</a> family.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hit_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-hit-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-debut_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-debut-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> Her mother, Asha Ranaut, is a school teacher, and her father, Amardeep Ranaut, is a businessman.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-biography_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-biography-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> She has an elder sister, Rangoli, who as of 2014 works as her manager, and a younger brother, Akshat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-think_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-think-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-peek_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-peek-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> Her great-grandfather, Sarju Singh Ranaut, was a <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_Legislative_Assembly_(India)" title="Member of the Legislative Assembly (India)">Member of the Legislative Assembly</a>, and her grandfather was an officer for the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Administrative_Service" title="Indian Administrative Service">Indian Administrative Service</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-toi_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-toi-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> She grew up in a <a href="/wiki/Hindu_joint_family" title="Hindu joint family">joint family</a> at their ancestral <a href="/wiki/Haveli" title="Haveli">haveli</a> (mansion) in Bhambla, and described her childhood as "simple and happy".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-peek_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-peek-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cosmo_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-cosmo-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>According to Ranaut, she was "stubborn and rebellious" while growing up: "If my father would gift my brother a plastic gun and get a doll for me, I would not accept that. I questioned the discrimination."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-htinterview_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-htinterview-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> She did not subscribe to the stereotypes that were expected of her, and experimented with fashion from a young age, often pairing up accessories and clothes that would seem "bizarre" to her neighbours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cosmo_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-cosmo-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-htinterview_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-htinterview-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> Ranaut was educated at the <a href="/wiki/Dayanand_Anglo-Vedic_Schools_System" title="Dayanand Anglo-Vedic Schools System">DAV School</a> in <a href="/wiki/Chandigarh" title="Chandigarh">Chandigarh</a>, where she pursued science as her core subject, remarking that she was "very studious" and "always paranoid about [...] results".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-swan_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-swan-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> She initially intended to become a doctor on the insistence of her parents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-doctor_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-doctor-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> However, a failed unit test in <a href="/wiki/Chemistry" title="Chemistry">chemistry</a> during her <a href="/wiki/Education_in_India" title="Education in India">twelfth grade</a> led Ranaut to reconsider her career prospects, and despite preparing for the <a href="/wiki/All_India_Pre_Medical_Test" title="All India Pre Medical Test">All India Pre Medical Test</a>, she did not turn up for the exam.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-doctor_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-doctor-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> Determined to find her "space and freedom", she relocated to <a href="/wiki/Delhi" title="Delhi">Delhi</a> at the age of sixteen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-think_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-think-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-soul_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-soul-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> Her decision not to pursue medicine led to constant feuding with her parents and her father refused to sponsor a pursuit he considered to be aimless.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-htinterview_9-2"><a href="#cite_note-htinterview-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In Delhi, Ranaut was unsure which career to choose; the <a href="/wiki/Elite_Model_Management" title="Elite Model Management">Elite Modelling Agency</a> were impressed by her looks and suggested that she model for them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-biography_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-biography-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-soul_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-soul-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> She took on a few modelling assignments, but generally disliked the career as she found "no scope for creativity".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-biography_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-biography-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-soul_13-2"><a href="#cite_note-soul-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> Ranaut decided to shift focus towards acting, and joined the Asmita Theatre Group, where she trained under the theatre director <a href="/wiki/Arvind_Gaur" title="Arvind Gaur">Arvind Gaur</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> She participated in Gaur's theatre workshop at the <a href="/wiki/India_Habitat_Centre" title="India Habitat Centre">India Habitat Centre</a>, acting in several of his plays, including the <a href="/wiki/Girish_Karnad" title="Girish Karnad">Girish Karnad</a>-scripted <i><a href="/wiki/Taledanda" title="Taledanda">Taledanda</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> During a screening when one of the male actors went missing, Ranaut played his part along with her original role of a woman.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hearts_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-hearts-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> A positive reaction from the audience prompted her to relocate to <a href="/wiki/Mumbai" title="Mumbai">Mumbai</a> to pursue a career in film, and she enrolled herself for a four-month acting course in Asha Chandra's drama school.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Ranaut struggled with her meager earnings during this period, eating only "bread and aachar (pickle)". Refusing her father's financial assistance led to a rift in their relationship which she later regretted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-toi_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-toi-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-htinterview_9-3"><a href="#cite_note-htinterview-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> Her relatives were unhappy with her decision to enter the film-making industry,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-think_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-think-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> and they did not correspond with her for several years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hit_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-hit-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-peek_6-2"><a href="#cite_note-peek-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-htinterview_9-4"><a href="#cite_note-htinterview-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> She reconciled with them after the release of <i><a href="/wiki/Life_in_a..._Metro" title="Life in a... Metro">Life in a... Metro</a></i> in 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-peek_6-3"><a href="#cite_note-peek-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Film_debut_and_critical_acclaim">Film debut and critical acclaim</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kangana_Ranaut_at_GIFA_in_2006.jpg"><img alt="Kangana Ranaut is smiling away from the camera" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="294" data-file-width="255" height="231" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Kangana_Ranaut_at_GIFA_in_2006.jpg/200px-Kangana_Ranaut_at_GIFA_in_2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/70/Kangana_Ranaut_at_GIFA_in_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/70/Kangana_Ranaut_at_GIFA_in_2006.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kangana_Ranaut_at_GIFA_in_2006.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ranaut at the 2006 <a href="/wiki/Global_Indian_Film_Awards" title="Global Indian Film Awards">Global Indian Film Awards</a> where she won the <a href="/wiki/GIFA_Best_Female_Debut_Award" title="GIFA Best Female Debut Award">Best Female Debut</a> award for <i><a href="/wiki/Gangster_(2006_film)" title="Gangster (2006 film)">Gangster</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gifa_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-gifa-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2004, the producers Ramesh Sharma and Pahlaj Nilani announced that Ranaut would make her film debut with the Deepak Shivdasani-directed <i>I Love You Boss</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-debut_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-debut-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-catch_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-catch-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> The following year, an agent took her to the office of the producer <a href="/wiki/Mahesh_Bhatt" title="Mahesh Bhatt">Mahesh Bhatt</a>, where she interacted with the director <a href="/wiki/Anurag_Basu" title="Anurag Basu">Anurag Basu</a> and auditioned for the lead role in the romantic thriller <i><a href="/wiki/Gangster_(2006_film)" title="Gangster (2006 film)">Gangster</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-soul_13-3"><a href="#cite_note-soul-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-loss_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-loss-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> Bhatt felt that she was too young for the role and signed <a href="/wiki/Chitrangada_Singh" title="Chitrangada Singh">Chitrangada Singh</a> instead. However, Singh was later unavailable to do the film, and Ranaut was contracted as a replacement for <i>Gangster,</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-loss_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-loss-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> opting out of <i>I Love You Boss</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-catch_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-catch-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> She was cast in the central role of Simran, an alcoholic woman caught in a romantic triangle between a notorious gangster (played by <a href="/wiki/Shiney_Ahuja" title="Shiney Ahuja">Shiney Ahuja</a>) and a sympathetic friend (played by <a href="/wiki/Emraan_Hashmi" title="Emraan Hashmi">Emraan Hashmi</a>). Ranaut was only seventeen while filming and said that she "had difficulty first in understanding and then unwinding from the character", describing her craft as "raw and immature".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-english_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-english-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> Released in 2006, <i>Gangster</i> emerged as a critical and commercial success and her performance was praised.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-journey_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-journey-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-box_office_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-box_office-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Raja_Sen" title="Raja Sen">Raja Sen</a> of <a href="/wiki/Rediff.com" title="Rediff.com">Rediff.com</a> said that "Kangana is a remarkable find, the actress coming across with great conviction. Hers is the pivotal character, and an extremely difficult role to essay, but she manages it well [...] Kangana's nuances [of an alcoholic character] are disconcertingly realistic."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> She won the <a href="/wiki/Filmfare_Award_for_Best_Female_Debut" title="Filmfare Award for Best Female Debut">Filmfare Award for Best Female Debut</a>, along with various other debut awards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bio_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-bio-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Ranaut's next role was in the <a href="/wiki/Mohit_Suri" title="Mohit Suri">Mohit Suri</a>-directed drama <i><a href="/wiki/Woh_Lamhe" title="Woh Lamhe">Woh Lamhe</a></i> (2006), a semi-biographical film based on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Schizophrenic" title="Schizophrenic">schizophrenic</a> actress <a href="/wiki/Parveen_Babi" title="Parveen Babi">Parveen Babi</a> and her relationship with the director Mahesh Bhatt.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> She said that portraying Babi had left her emotionally drained, as she had begun to "feel her desolation and loneliness."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> Film critic <a href="/wiki/Subhash_K._Jha" title="Subhash K. Jha">Subhash K. Jha</a> wrote that Ranaut "is the first female performer of Bollywood since <a href="/wiki/Smita_Patil" title="Smita Patil">Smita</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shabana_Azmi" title="Shabana Azmi">Shabana</a> who isn't scared to strip her soul naked for the camera", adding that she is a "hugely expressive actress with a phemomenal ability to convey torment, hurt and incredulity through the eyes".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> Despite positive reviews, the film underperformed at the box office.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The following year, Ranaut portrayed an aspiring musician in <a href="/wiki/Suneel_Darshan" title="Suneel Darshan">Suneel Darshan</a>'s musical thriller <i><a href="/wiki/Shakalaka_Boom_Boom" title="Shakalaka Boom Boom">Shakalaka Boom Boom</a></i>, alongside <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Deol" title="Bobby Deol">Bobby Deol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Upen_Patel" title="Upen Patel">Upen Patel</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Celina_Jaitley" title="Celina Jaitley">Celina Jaitley</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> The film's production was marred by a dispute between Ranaut and Darshan; she objected to her voice being dubbed by another artist, but he insisted that he needed a particular "twang and accent" for her character.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/India_Today" title="India Today">India Today</a></i> described the film as an "amateur mess", and the film proved to be a box office flop.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-box_office_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-box_office-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> She next reunited with Anurag Basu for the <a href="/wiki/Ensemble_cast" title="Ensemble cast">ensemble</a> drama <i>Life in a... Metro</i>, playing the supporting role of Neha, a shrewd socialite engaged in an affair with her married boss (played by <a href="/wiki/Kay_Kay_Menon" title="Kay Kay Menon">Kay Kay Menon</a>). Despite a poor initial run at the box office, the film emerged as a profitable venture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Khalid_Mohamed" title="Khalid Mohamed">Khalid Mohamed</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/Hindustan_Times" title="Hindustan Times">Hindustan Times</a></i> was critical of the film, noting its lack of originality and realism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> In a more positive review, Raja Sen wrote that Ranaut "is refreshing [...] and manages to herd her emotions well, playing a complex role but hardly ever overreaching", but criticised her delivery of English lines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> For her role, Ranaut was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Stardust_Award_for_Breakthrough_Performance_%E2%80%93_Female" title="Stardust Award for Breakthrough Performance – Female">Stardust Award for Breakthrough Performance – Female</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bio_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-bio-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Ranaut next portrayed a village girl in <i><a href="/wiki/Dhaam_Dhoom" title="Dhaam Dhoom">Dhaam Dhoom</a></i> (2008), a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Tamil_Nadu" title="Cinema of Tamil Nadu">Tamil</a> romantic thriller, opposite <a href="/wiki/Jayam_Ravi" title="Jayam Ravi">Jayam Ravi</a>. Production on the film was temporarily halted when the director, <a href="/wiki/Jeeva_(director)" title="Jeeva (director)">Jeeva</a>, died of cardiac arrest, and the film was completed by the crew members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> A review carried by <i><a href="/wiki/Post_(South_Africa)" title="Post (South Africa)">Post</a></i> wrote that Ranaut had "little scope" in a role that did not suit her.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>India Today</i> described her next film, the <a href="/wiki/Madhur_Bhandarkar" title="Madhur Bhandarkar">Madhur Bhandarkar</a>-directed drama <i><a href="/wiki/Fashion_(film)" title="Fashion (film)">Fashion</a></i> (2008), as a "landmark" in her career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-journey_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-journey-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> Set against the backdrop of the Indian fashion industry, the film co-starred <a href="/wiki/Priyanka_Chopra" title="Priyanka Chopra">Priyanka Chopra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mugdha_Godse" title="Mugdha Godse">Mugdha Godse</a>, and featured Ranaut as Shonali Gujral, a <a href="/wiki/Substance_dependence" title="Substance dependence">substance abusing</a> supermodel struggling to cope with her foundering career. Because the media speculated that her role was based on the former model Geetanjali Nagpal (which both Ranaut and Bhandarkar denied),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> the Delhi Commission for Women (DCW) ordered a stay on the film's release, approving it only after a script narration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-A_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-A-40"><span>[</span>a<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> With a worldwide revenue of 600 million Indian rupees (<img alt="INR" data-file-height="754" data-file-width="512" height="10" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Indian_Rupee_symbol.svg/7px-Indian_Rupee_symbol.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Indian_Rupee_symbol.svg/11px-Indian_Rupee_symbol.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Indian_Rupee_symbol.svg/14px-Indian_Rupee_symbol.svg.png 2x" style="vertical-align: baseline" width="7"/>), approximately US$10 million, <i>Fashion</i> emerged as a commercial success,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> and was listed by Subhash K. Jha as one of the best films of the decade with women protagonists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> Ranaut's performance drew unanimous critical acclaim.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-journey_22-2"><a href="#cite_note-journey-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Taran_Adarsh" title="Taran Adarsh">Taran Adarsh</a> of <a href="/wiki/Bollywood_Hungama" title="Bollywood Hungama">Bollywood Hungama</a> praised her confident portrayal of the character and believed that she was the real star of the film,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Nikhat_Kazmi" title="Nikhat Kazmi">Nikhat Kazmi</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times_of_India" title="The Times of India">The Times of India</a></i> added that she "does an exquisite metamorphosis from a wispy, high-strung, nervous child-woman to a stunning ramp diva."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> Her portrayal earned Ranaut several awards, including the <a href="/wiki/National_Film_Award_for_Best_Supporting_Actress" title="National Film Award for Best Supporting Actress">National Film Award</a> and <a href="/wiki/Filmfare_Award_for_Best_Supporting_Actress" title="Filmfare Award for Best Supporting Actress">Filmfare Award</a> for Best Supporting Actress.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bio_25-2"><a href="#cite_note-bio-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Career_fluctuations">Career fluctuations</span></h3>
<p>The supernatural horror film <i><a href="/wiki/Raaz:_The_Mystery_Continues" title="Raaz: The Mystery Continues">Raaz: The Mystery Continues</a></i> from director Mohit Suri was Ranaut's first film release of 2009, in which she played a successful model who is possessed by a ghost.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> The film co-starred Emraan Hashmi and <a href="/wiki/Adhyayan_Suman" title="Adhyayan Suman">Adhyayan Suman</a>, and proved to be a financial success.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-box_office_23-2"><a href="#cite_note-box_office-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> Shubhra Gupta of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Indian_Express" title="The Indian Express">The Indian Express</a></i> noted that Ranaut was becoming stereotyped in roles that required her to be "hysterical", adding that she needed a "radical change of image".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> Also that year, she played the <a href="/wiki/Leading_lady" title="Leading lady">leading lady</a> in the drama <i><a href="/wiki/Vaada_Raha" title="Vaada Raha">Vaada Raha</a></i> and the <a href="/wiki/Telugu_cinema" title="Telugu cinema">Telugu</a> action film <i><a href="/wiki/Ek_Niranjan" title="Ek Niranjan">Ek Niranjan</a></i>, neither of which were particularly notable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-journey_22-3"><a href="#cite_note-journey-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kangna_Ranaut_and_R_Madhavan_promote_%27Tanu_Weds_Manu%27_on_Jhalak_Dikhhla_Jaa_sets.jpg"><img alt="Kangana Ranaut and R. Madhavan pose for the camera" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="417" data-file-width="355" height="235" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Kangna_Ranaut_and_R_Madhavan_promote_%27Tanu_Weds_Manu%27_on_Jhalak_Dikhhla_Jaa_sets.jpg/200px-Kangna_Ranaut_and_R_Madhavan_promote_%27Tanu_Weds_Manu%27_on_Jhalak_Dikhhla_Jaa_sets.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Kangna_Ranaut_and_R_Madhavan_promote_%27Tanu_Weds_Manu%27_on_Jhalak_Dikhhla_Jaa_sets.jpg/300px-Kangna_Ranaut_and_R_Madhavan_promote_%27Tanu_Weds_Manu%27_on_Jhalak_Dikhhla_Jaa_sets.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/60/Kangna_Ranaut_and_R_Madhavan_promote_%27Tanu_Weds_Manu%27_on_Jhalak_Dikhhla_Jaa_sets.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kangna_Ranaut_and_R_Madhavan_promote_%27Tanu_Weds_Manu%27_on_Jhalak_Dikhhla_Jaa_sets.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ranaut with co-star <a href="/wiki/R._Madhavan" title="R. Madhavan">R. Madhavan</a> at a promotional event for <i><a href="/wiki/Tanu_Weds_Manu" title="Tanu Weds Manu">Tanu Weds Manu</a></i>, 2011</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In a brief role in Anurag Basu's romantic thriller <i><a href="/wiki/Kites_(film)" title="Kites (film)">Kites</a></i> (2010), Ranaut portrayed the fiancée of <a href="/wiki/Hrithik_Roshan" title="Hrithik Roshan">Hrithik Roshan</a>'s character. She said that she felt "cheated" after watching the film, as her role proved to be much smaller than what she had initially signed on for.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-starweek_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-starweek-48"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> She then portrayed fictional film actress Rehana in the <a href="/wiki/Milan_Luthria" title="Milan Luthria">Milan Luthria</a>-directed gangster film <i><a href="/wiki/Once_Upon_a_Time_in_Mumbaai" title="Once Upon a Time in Mumbaai">Once Upon a Time in Mumbaai</a></i>. Also starring <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ajay_Devgn" title="Ajay Devgn">Ajay Devgn</a>, Emraan Hashmi and <a href="/wiki/Prachi_Desai" title="Prachi Desai">Prachi Desai</a>, the film chronicles the rise and subsequent fall of an underworld don (played by Devgn) in the 1970s. Ranaut said that her character was "a mix" of the actress <a href="/wiki/Madhubala" title="Madhubala">Madhubala</a> and the gangster <a href="/wiki/Haji_Mastan" title="Haji Mastan">Haji Mastan</a>'s wife, and that to prepare she observed the work of the actresses <a href="/wiki/Zeenat_Aman" title="Zeenat Aman">Zeenat Aman</a> and Parveen Babi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> The film was one of the most successful releases of the year, and garnered positive reviews from critics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> Sudish Kamath of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hindu" title="The Hindu">The Hindu</a></i> labelled her a "delight" and <i><a href="/wiki/Mid_Day" title="Mid Day">Mid Day</a></i> '​s Sarita Tanwar praised her for being "totally convincing" in the role.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> After playing a television reporter in the thriller <i><a href="/wiki/Knock_Out_(2010_film)" title="Knock Out (2010 film)">Knock Out</a></i>, Ranaut actively looked for a comedy and found the role in <a href="/wiki/Anees_Bazmee" title="Anees Bazmee">Anees Bazmee</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/No_Problem_(2010_film)" title="No Problem (2010 film)">No Problem</a></i>, but both films failed to propel her career forward.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-journey_22-4"><a href="#cite_note-journey-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>According to Bollywood Hungama, after establishing a reputation for portraying <a href="/wiki/Neurosis" title="Neurosis">neurotic</a> characters, Ranaut was seeking projects that would be "less emotionally exhausting" for her.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> Her first release of 2011 was <a href="/wiki/Anand_L._Rai" title="Anand L. Rai">Anand L. Rai</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Tanu_Weds_Manu" title="Tanu Weds Manu">Tanu Weds Manu</a></i>, a romantic comedy opposite <a href="/wiki/R._Madhavan" title="R. Madhavan">R. Madhavan</a>, which Ranaut considers a "game changer" for her.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> Rai stated that he cast her for the role to illustrate that the actress was capable of playing other roles and that her character in the film was unlike any of those that she had played previously.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> Critical reaction to the film was mixed, though Ranaut's performance was praised.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-box_office_23-3"><a href="#cite_note-box_office-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bio_25-3"><a href="#cite_note-bio-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rajeev_Masand" title="Rajeev Masand">Rajeev Masand</a> wrote, "Kangana Ranaut is a pleasant surprise in a cheery, upbeat part that we haven't seen her take on before. She rises to the challenge, only hampered occasionally by her mangled dialogue delivery."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> Ranaut received Best Actress nominations at several award ceremonies, including <a href="/wiki/Screen_Awards" title="Screen Awards">Screen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zee_Cine_Awards" title="Zee Cine Awards">Zee Cine</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Ranaut followed the success of <i>Tanu Weds Manu</i> by starring in a series of brief, glamorous roles in four other films of 2011: <i><a href="/wiki/Game_(2011_film)" title="Game (2011 film)">Game</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Double_Dhamaal" title="Double Dhamaal">Double Dhamaal</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Rascals_(film)" title="Rascals (film)">Rascals</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Miley_Naa_Miley_Hum" title="Miley Naa Miley Hum">Miley Naa Miley Hum</a></i>. With the exception of <i>Double Dhamaal</i>, none of these films performed well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-journey_22-5"><a href="#cite_note-journey-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-box_office_23-4"><a href="#cite_note-box_office-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> In a review for <i>Rascals</i>, the critic Gaurav Malani wrote: "Kangana Ranaut is ill at ease in comedy. She struggles to hold her own and emerges as a bimbo in her act."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> Ranaut later said that she did some of these films due to a dearth of film offers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rejection_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-rejection-65"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> The following year, Ranaut portrayed a supporting role opposite Ajay Devgn in <a href="/wiki/Priyadarshan" title="Priyadarshan">Priyadarshan</a>'s action thriller <i><a href="/wiki/Tezz" title="Tezz">Tezz</a></i>, another box office flop.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-box_office_23-5"><a href="#cite_note-box_office-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2013_onwards">2013 onwards</span></h3>
<p>The director <a href="/wiki/Sanjay_Gupta_(director)" title="Sanjay Gupta (director)">Sanjay Gupta</a> cast Ranaut in a brief role opposite <a href="/wiki/John_Abraham_(actor)" title="John Abraham (actor)">John Abraham</a> in the crime thriller <i><a href="/wiki/Shootout_at_Wadala" title="Shootout at Wadala">Shootout at Wadala</a></i> (2013) due to her ability to stand out in a predominantly male-centric film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_News_and_Analysis" title="Daily News and Analysis">Daily News and Analysis</a></i> '​ Tushar Joshi wrote that her role was written "to provide the sex quotient", and critic Vinayak Chakravorty opined that she "does not get much scope [...] beyond the steamy lovemaking grind".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> Commercially, the film performed moderately well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-box_office_23-6"><a href="#cite_note-box_office-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kangana_Ranaut_at_QUEEN_success_party.jpg"><img alt="Kangana Ranaut is looking away from the camera" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="409" data-file-width="244" height="285" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Kangana_Ranaut_at_QUEEN_success_party.jpg/170px-Kangana_Ranaut_at_QUEEN_success_party.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b6/Kangana_Ranaut_at_QUEEN_success_party.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b6/Kangana_Ranaut_at_QUEEN_success_party.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kangana_Ranaut_at_QUEEN_success_party.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ranaut at the success party of <i><a href="/wiki/Queen_(film)" title="Queen (film)">Queen</a></i> (2014). She won the <a href="/wiki/Filmfare_Award_for_Best_Actress" title="Filmfare Award for Best Actress">Filmfare Award for Best Actress</a> for the film</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Ranaut achieved success later in 2013 for her portrayal of Kaya, a <a href="/wiki/Shapeshifting" title="Shapeshifting">shapeshifting</a> <a href="/wiki/Mutant" title="Mutant">mutant</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Rakesh_Roshan" title="Rakesh Roshan">Rakesh Roshan</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Science_fiction_film" title="Science fiction film">science fiction</a> film <i><a href="/wiki/Krrish_3" title="Krrish 3">Krrish 3</a></i>, alongside Hrithik Roshan, Priyanka Chopra and <a href="/wiki/Vivek_Oberoi" title="Vivek Oberoi">Vivek Oberoi</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> When Rakesh Roshan first offered the role to her, she declined it due a disappointing prior association with him on <i>Kites</i>, in which Roshan had served as producer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-starweek_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-starweek-48"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> Following Ranaut's rejection, other actresses also turned down the role.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> Roshan approached her again, and after assuring her that the role would not be a minuscule one, Ranaut accepted the part.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-starweek_48-2"><a href="#cite_note-starweek-48"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> Critics thought that <i>Krrish 3</i> was entertaining but lacking in originality, though Ranaut's performance garnered praise.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-journey_22-6"><a href="#cite_note-journey-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> The critic Sarita Tanwar of <i>Daily News and Analysis</i> said: "Kangana Ranaut is delightful as an alien making the weird hair and clothes work for her. She even manages to make you feel her pain. Quite an accomplishment that!"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> With global ticket sales of <span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Indian_rupee" title="Indian rupee"><img alt="INR" data-file-height="754" data-file-width="512" height="10" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Indian_Rupee_symbol.svg/7px-Indian_Rupee_symbol.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Indian_Rupee_symbol.svg/11px-Indian_Rupee_symbol.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Indian_Rupee_symbol.svg/14px-Indian_Rupee_symbol.svg.png 2x" style="vertical-align: baseline" width="7"/></a>3 billion</span> (US$47 million), the film emerged as one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_Bollywood_films" title="List of highest-grossing Bollywood films">highest-grossing Bollywood films of all time</a>, becoming Ranaut's most financially profitable venture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-box_office_23-7"><a href="#cite_note-box_office-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> Also that year, Ranaut played the eponymous lead in the musical drama <i><a href="/wiki/Rajjo" title="Rajjo">Rajjo</a></i>. The film was a critical and commercial failure and Ranaut's portrayal of a <a href="/wiki/Nautch" title="Nautch">nautch girl</a> was largely criticised.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-box_office_23-8"><a href="#cite_note-box_office-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> Paloma Sharma of Rediff.com commented that "Kangana Ranaut struggles with her <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mumbaiyya" title="Mumbaiyya">Mumbaiyya</a> dialogues and is not as graceful in the dance sequences as one would have expected."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 2014, Ranaut established herself as a leading actress of contemporary Hindi cinema when she featured alongside <a href="/wiki/Rajkummar_Rao" title="Rajkummar Rao">Rajkummar Rao</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lisa_Haydon" title="Lisa Haydon">Lisa Haydon</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Coming-of-age_story" title="Coming-of-age story">coming-of-age</a> dramedy <i><a href="/wiki/Queen_(film)" title="Queen (film)">Queen</a></i>; she also co-wrote the dialogues with <a href="/wiki/Anvita_Dutt_Guptan" title="Anvita Dutt Guptan">Anvita Dutt Guptan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> The film tells the story of Rani, a naive girl who embarks on her honeymoon alone after her fiancé calls off their wedding. Ranaut, who describes herself as "independent and confident", reflected that the role was one of the toughest she had played, as the character's personality traits contrasted with her own.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> The film and Ranaut's performance received unanimous acclaim from critics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> Devesh Sharma of <i><a href="/wiki/Filmfare" title="Filmfare">Filmfare</a></i> wrote that the fact that she "flits from one aspect of her character to another without breaking stride shows her maturity as an actor. Her efforts make you clap for Rani's small and big victories, you root for her character to come up trumps and are glad about the glorious transformation at the end."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> With a worldwide total of <span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Indian_rupee" title="Indian rupee"><img alt="INR" data-file-height="754" data-file-width="512" height="10" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Indian_Rupee_symbol.svg/7px-Indian_Rupee_symbol.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Indian_Rupee_symbol.svg/11px-Indian_Rupee_symbol.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Indian_Rupee_symbol.svg/14px-Indian_Rupee_symbol.svg.png 2x" style="vertical-align: baseline" width="7"/></a>970 million</span> (US$15 million), the film also emerged as a box office hit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-box_office_23-9"><a href="#cite_note-box_office-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> She won the <a href="/wiki/Filmfare_Award_for_Best_Actress" title="Filmfare Award for Best Actress">Filmfare Award for Best Actress</a> for the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ff15_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-ff15-86"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> Ranaut next played Alka Singh, an aggressive politician with a criminal record, in the black comedy <i><a href="/wiki/Revolver_Rani" title="Revolver Rani">Revolver Rani</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> Critics expressed mixed views on the film, but were appreciative of Ranaut's performance, which Madhureeta Mukherjee of <i>The Times of India</i> described as "pure dynamite".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> Later that year, Ranaut played the brief role of a medical intern who moonlights as a member of a vigilante group in the <a href="/wiki/Karan_Johar" title="Karan Johar">Karan Johar</a>-produced political drama <i><a href="/wiki/Ungli" title="Ungli">Ungli</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Upcoming_projects">Upcoming projects</span></h4>
<p>As of January 2015, Ranaut has completed work on <i><a href="/wiki/I_Love_New_Year" title="I Love New Year">I Love New Year</a></i>, a romantic comedy with <a href="/wiki/Sunny_Deol" title="Sunny Deol">Sunny Deol</a>, which after numerous delays is awaiting release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> Ranaut is filming a sequel to <i>Tanu Weds Manu</i>, entitled <i><a href="/wiki/Tanu_Weds_Manu_Returns" title="Tanu Weds Manu Returns">Tanu Weds Manu Returns</a></i>, in which she will portray dual roles; she will reprise the character of Tanuja from the original and also portray a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haryanvi" title="Haryanvi">Haryanvi</a> athlete.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> She is also filming opposite <a href="/wiki/Imran_Khan_(actor)" title="Imran Khan (actor)">Imran Khan</a> for <i><a href="/wiki/Katti_Batti" title="Katti Batti">Katti Batti</a></i>, a romantic comedy directed by <a href="/wiki/Nikhil_Advani" title="Nikhil Advani">Nikhil Advani</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition, she has been cast for Sai Kabir's <i>Divine Lovers</i>, an Indian-French co-production about corruption co-starring <a href="/wiki/Irrfan_Khan" title="Irrfan Khan">Irrfan Khan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reema_Kagti" title="Reema Kagti">Reema Kagti</a>'s romance film <i>Mr. Chaalu</i> opposite <a href="/wiki/Shahid_Kapoor" title="Shahid Kapoor">Shahid Kapoor</a>, and an untitled project on mountaineering from the director <a href="/wiki/Hansal_Mehta" title="Hansal Mehta">Hansal Mehta</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> Ranaut will also be making her production and directorial debut with an English language short film entitled <i>The Touch</i>, dealing with the relationship between a four-year old boy and a dog; she co-wrote the screenplay with an Australian writer and completed principal photography in America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kangana_Ranaut.jpg"><img alt="Kangana Ranaut is walking the ramp" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="563" data-file-width="319" height="388" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Kangana_Ranaut.jpg/220px-Kangana_Ranaut.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e9/Kangana_Ranaut.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e9/Kangana_Ranaut.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kangana_Ranaut.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ranaut at the 2011 <a href="/wiki/Femina_Miss_India" title="Femina Miss India">Femina Miss India</a> ceremony</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Ranaut has stated that her initial years in the film industry were marred with difficulties as she was unprepared to be an actress.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-english_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-english-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> She was conscious of her poor command of the English language, and struggled to "fit in".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-english_21-2"><a href="#cite_note-english-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> In a 2013 interview with <i>Daily News and Analysis</i>, Ranaut recollected:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>"People in the industry treated me like I didn't deserve to be spoken to and I was some unwanted object. I couldn't speak English fluently and people made fun of me for that. So dealing with rejection became a part of life. [...] All that has taken a toll, I guess. I find it hard to deal with praise. Today, when people say that I have made it and made it on my own, I feel like locking up myself somewhere... It scares me."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-treat_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-treat-99"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>During the struggle, Ranaut found support in the actor <a href="/wiki/Aditya_Pancholi" title="Aditya Pancholi">Aditya Pancholi</a> and his wife <a href="/wiki/Zarina_Wahab" title="Zarina Wahab">Zarina Wahab</a>, and considered them her "family away from home".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-treat_99-1"><a href="#cite_note-treat-99"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup> She was embroiled in a well publicised scandal when the media speculated on the nature of her relationship with Pancholi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> She declined to speak about it openly, though made several public appearances with him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2007 it was reported that Ranaut had filed a police complaint against Pancholi for physically assaulting her under the influence of alcohol.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> The following year Pancholi confirmed the affair in an interview, saying that he had been cohabiting with Ranaut in the past, and accused her of owing him <span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Indian_rupee" title="Indian rupee"><img alt="INR" data-file-height="754" data-file-width="512" height="10" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Indian_Rupee_symbol.svg/7px-Indian_Rupee_symbol.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Indian_Rupee_symbol.svg/11px-Indian_Rupee_symbol.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Indian_Rupee_symbol.svg/14px-Indian_Rupee_symbol.svg.png 2x" style="vertical-align: baseline" width="7"/></a>2.5 million</span> (US$39,000).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-money_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-money-104"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> In response, Ranaut's spokesperson said that "[a]fter physically assaulting her in the middle of a road, he has no right to expect anything from her", adding that she had "already given <span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Indian_rupee" title="Indian rupee"><img alt="INR" data-file-height="754" data-file-width="512" height="10" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Indian_Rupee_symbol.svg/7px-Indian_Rupee_symbol.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Indian_Rupee_symbol.svg/11px-Indian_Rupee_symbol.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Indian_Rupee_symbol.svg/14px-Indian_Rupee_symbol.svg.png 2x" style="vertical-align: baseline" width="7"/></a>5 million</span> (US$79,000) to [him] as a goodwill gesture".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-money_104-1"><a href="#cite_note-money-104"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> Ranaut later said that the incident had left her "physically and mentally" damaged.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-htinterview_9-5"><a href="#cite_note-htinterview-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>While filming <i>Raaz: The Mystery Continues</i> in 2008, Ranaut began a romantic relationship with co-star Adhyayan Suman.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> On Suman's insistence that he focus on his professional career, the couple separated the following year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> From 2010 to 2012, Ranaut was involved in a long-distance romance with Nicholas Lafferty, an English doctor;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-marry_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-marry-107"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> she described the relationship as "the most normal" she ever had, but the couple split amicably as she was not ready for marriage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-english_21-3"><a href="#cite_note-english-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-treat_99-2"><a href="#cite_note-treat-99"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup> She has since maintained that she will never get married,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-english_21-4"><a href="#cite_note-english-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-marry_107-1"><a href="#cite_note-marry-107"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> and has expressed a desire to not be bound by a relationship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Ranaut lives in Mumbai with her sister Rangoli, who was the victim of an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Acid_attack" title="Acid attack">acid attack</a> in 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> She makes yearly visits to her hometown of Bhambla.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-htinterview_9-6"><a href="#cite_note-htinterview-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> A practicing <a href="/wiki/Hindu" title="Hindu">Hindu</a>, Ranaut follows the teachings of the spiritual leader <a href="/wiki/Swami_Vivekananda" title="Swami Vivekananda">Swami Vivekananda</a> and considers meditation to be "the highest form of worshipping God".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> She practices vegetarianism and was listed as "India's hottest vegetarian" in a poll conducted by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PETA" title="PETA">PETA</a> in 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> Since 2009 Ranaut has been studying the dance form of <a href="/wiki/Kathak" title="Kathak">kathak</a> from the Nateshwar Nritya Kala Mandir.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> She has said that the technical process of filmmaking is of tremendous interest to her,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> and to better her understanding of it Ranaut enrolled in a two-month screenplay writing course at the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Film_Academy" title="New York Film Academy">New York Film Academy</a> in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup> In an interview with <i>Filmfare</i> she said that despite her stardom, she wants to lead a normal life: "I don't want to lose my rights as a common person to learn and grow".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rejection_65-1"><a href="#cite_note-rejection-65"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_the_media">In the media</span></h2>
<p>In the book <i>Acting Smart: Your Ticket to Showbiz</i>, <a href="/wiki/Tisca_Chopra" title="Tisca Chopra">Tisca Chopra</a> describes Ranaut as a "free-spirited, original creative" person "who cannot really be slotted in a particular mould".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chopra2014_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chopra2014-117"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> Ranaut is particularly known for her forthrightness in expressing her opinions in public on issues ranging from film to feminism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-think_5-3"><a href="#cite_note-think-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hornet_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-hornet-118"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> A televised interview hosted by <a href="/wiki/Anupama_Chopra" title="Anupama Chopra">Anupama Chopra</a> in which Ranaut spoke out against gender bias and nepotism in Bollywood went <a href="/wiki/Viral_video" title="Viral video">viral</a> online, which led Sunaina Kumar of <i><a href="/wiki/Tehelka" title="Tehelka">Tehelka</a></i> to write: "In this age of cookie-cutter heroines with stock responses, Kangana Ranaut is refreshingly real and honest."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hornet_118-1"><a href="#cite_note-hornet-118"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kangna_at_Venky%27s_Mumbai_Fighters_versus_Bangkok_Elephants_match_03.jpg"><img alt="Kangana Ranaut is looking directly at the camera" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="439" data-file-width="585" height="195" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Kangna_at_Venky%27s_Mumbai_Fighters_versus_Bangkok_Elephants_match_03.jpg/260px-Kangna_at_Venky%27s_Mumbai_Fighters_versus_Bangkok_Elephants_match_03.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Kangna_at_Venky%27s_Mumbai_Fighters_versus_Bangkok_Elephants_match_03.jpg/390px-Kangna_at_Venky%27s_Mumbai_Fighters_versus_Bangkok_Elephants_match_03.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Kangna_at_Venky%27s_Mumbai_Fighters_versus_Bangkok_Elephants_match_03.jpg/520px-Kangna_at_Venky%27s_Mumbai_Fighters_versus_Bangkok_Elephants_match_03.jpg 2x" width="260"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kangna_at_Venky%27s_Mumbai_Fighters_versus_Bangkok_Elephants_match_03.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ranaut at an event for <a href="/wiki/Venky%27s" title="Venky's">Venky's</a> in 2012</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Analysing Ranaut's career, the journalist Parmita Uniyal, in 2014, noted that she "loves to challenge herself with tricky roles and manages to add a different dimension to her character every time."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hearts_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-hearts-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> A reviewer for Rediff.com described her as a "director's actress" who is susceptible to both "shine and crumble under the right/wrong guidance".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup> Anand L Rai (the director of <i>Tanu Weds Manu</i>) says that Ranaut actively pursues roles in which she can "work in her own space and not become a mere prop in the male-dominated Bollywood".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hearts_16-2"><a href="#cite_note-hearts-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> Alongside actress <a href="/wiki/Vidya_Balan" title="Vidya Balan">Vidya Balan</a>, Ranaut has been credited for spearheading a movement that breaks stereotypes of a Hindi film heroine by playing the protagonist in films (most notably <i>Queen</i>) not starring a well-known male star.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Ranaut is considered a sex symbol and a style icon in India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gq_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-gq-121"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> Analysing Ranaut's off-screen persona, <i>Hindustan Times</i> published that she was initially written off by Indian journalists due to her "funny accent" and the negative publicity generated by her troubled relationships; however, her defining fashion choices and her unconventional film roles eventually established her as a star.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup> Ranaut has frequently featured in listings of the most attractive and stylish celebrities in India. She held the ninth position on <i>The Times of India</i> '​s listing of the "Most Desirable Woman" in 2010, 2011 and 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> Ranaut was featured on <i><a href="/wiki/Verve_(magazine)" title="Verve (magazine)">Verve</a></i> '​s listing of the most powerful women of 2010, and in 2012 she was named the "Best Dressed Personality" by the Indian edition of <i><a href="/wiki/People_(magazine)" title="People (magazine)">People</a></i> magazine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2013, Ranaut featured as one of the best-dressed women celebrities by <i><a href="/wiki/Vogue_India" title="Vogue India">Vogue India</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup> The journalist Jagmeeta Thind Joy credits the actress for her "quirky, almost non-Bollywood take on personal style", adding that she "likes to shock and awe with her choices".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-swan_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-swan-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Selected_filmography">Selected filmography</span></h3>
<div class="div-col columns column-count column-count-2" style="-moz-column-count: 2; -webkit-column-count: 2; column-count: 2;">

</ul>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards">Awards</span></h3>
<p>Ranaut has been the recipient of a <a href="/wiki/National_Film_Awards_(India)" title="National Film Awards (India)">National Film Award</a> in the Best Supporting Actress category for <i>Fashion</i> (2008), and three <a href="/wiki/Filmfare_Awards" title="Filmfare Awards">Filmfare Awards</a>: Best Female Debut for <i>Gangster</i> (2006), Best Supporting Actress for <i>Fashion</i>, and Best Actress for <i>Queen</i> (2014).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bio_25-4"><a href="#cite_note-bio-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ff15_86-1"><a href="#cite_note-ff15-86"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span></h2>

<li id="cite_note-A-40"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-A_40-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Geetanjali Nagpal was a controversial model in the 1990s whose substance abuse led her to the streets of <a href="/wiki/Delhi" title="Delhi">Delhi</a>. The DCW, who had represented her during court proceedings and helped her recovery through <a href="/wiki/Drug_rehabilitation" title="Drug rehabilitation">rehabilitation</a>, was concerned that a negative depiction of her life would "affect her physical or mental health adversely".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
</ol>
